The Language of Wi’īian

Natively known as: Wi’ī /ˈwiʔiː/

...and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind...
za boˑsā riˑ xōmekeˑ hē ziwu za xē hē xēsā xiˑri beˑ kīhī
Pronunciation: /za ˈboˑsaː riˑ ɣoːˈmekeˑ heː ˈziwu za ɣeː heː ˈɣeːsaː ˈɣiˑri beˑ ˈkiːhiː/
Wi’īian word order: and stood he holding hat his and turned his face wet to the wind

Spelling & Phonology

Consonant inventory: /b d h j k l m p r s t w z ɣ ʔ/

Syllable structure: (C)V
Stress pattern: Penultimate — stress is on the second last syllable
Word initial consonants: b, d, h, j, k, l, m, p, r, s, t, w, z, ɣ, ʔ
Mid-word consonants: b, d, h, j, k, l, m, p, r, s, t, w, z, ɣ, ʔ
Word final consonants: N/A

Phonological rules (in order of application):

  • l → ɫ / V_V
Spelling rules:

PronunciationSpelling
j y
ɣ x
ʉ ǔ
ʌ ù
ʔ ’
ː macron over vowel

Grammar

Main word order: Verb-Subject-Object-Oblique. "Mary opened the door with a key" turns into Opened Mary the door with a key.
Adjective order: Adjectives are positioned after the noun.
Adposition: prepositions

Noun

Singular No affix
hēri /ˈheːri/
Plural Prefix di-
dihēri /diˈheːri/

Nouns have three cases:
Ergative is the doer of a verb: dog bites man
The ergative affix only appears if there is an absolutive in the sentence
Absolutive is the done-to of a verb: man bites dog
Absolutives are always no affix
Genitive is the possessor of something: dog’s tail hits man

Ergative Suffix -liˑ
hēriliˑ /heːˈriliˑ/
Absolutive No affix
hēri /ˈheːri/
Genitive Suffix -siˑ
hērisiˑ /heːˈrisiˑ/

the		 lī /liː/
some

Verbs

Present Suffix -keˑ
wezīwukeˑ /ˌweziːˈwukeˑ/
Past Suffix -seː
wezīwusē /ˌweziːˈwuseː/
Future Suffix -ziː
wezīwuzī /ˌweziːˈwuziː/

Imperfective aspect

The ‘imperfective’ aspect refers to ongoing actions, such as I am studying,
and habitual actions, such as I study (every night).

It is indicated with the affix:

Imperfect Suffix -da
wezīwuda /ˌweziːˈwuda/

Perfect aspect

Perfect aspect in English is exemplified in ‘I have read this book’,
which expresses an event that took place before the time spoken
but which has an effect on or is in some way still relevant to the present.

In Wi’īian, the perfect is constructed with the word for ‘finish’ ɣoːwuːmuˑ + present tense of the verb.

Derivational morphology

Adjective → noun = Prefix ʔo-
Noun → adjective = Prefix la-
Noun → verb = Prefix zeˑ-
Verb → noun = Prefix ʔa-
Verb → adjective = Prefix hiˑ-
Adjective → verb = Prefix ma-
Adjective → adverb = Prefix ɣiˑ-
One who Xs (e.g. paint → painter) = Prefix ʔuː-
Place of (e.g. wine → winery) = Prefix ziː-
Diminutive = Prefix soː-
Augmentative = Prefix zo-
